# Samuel Thomas Wilson  —  *Captain America (formerly and currently); the Falcon*

![[_attachments/sam_wilson.png]]

# Sam Wilson — UATU INTELLIGENCE DOSSIER

*Full-existence intelligence briefing. Independent, evidence-based assessment — the benevolent inverse of total surveillance.*


## Executive Brief (BLUF)

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: SAMUEL THOMAS WILSON
## EXECUTIVE BRIEF (BLUF)

---

### Bottom Line Up Front

**Subject is a high-functioning, unenhanced human adult, Black male, late-stage operational career, presenting as one of the most psychologically integrated principals in the enhanced-actor population — and that integration is itself the achievement, not the baseline.** The dossier reads, at first pass, as anomalously clean: no substance use, no Axis I disorder, durable adult attachments, a track record of de-escalation across a fifty-year operational tail, and a stress-response curve that flattens upward rather than spiking into aggression. The anomaly resolves when one notes that *every* element of his presentation is the product of deliberate, sustained, daily self-construction against a life history that statistically should have produced a much more damaged man. Subject is not unwounded; subject is *unceasingly metabolizing* a wound that has never closed and is not expected to close. The operational tempo of that metabolization is the single most important variable in his file.

The shortest accurate description of the subject is this: **a man who has been told, repeatedly and by powerful actors, who he "really" is — and who has answered, each time, by continuing to be who he has decided to be.** Everything else in the file is downstream of that sentence.

---

### Who He Is At The Deepest Level

Strip away the wings, the shield, the costume nomenclature, the team affiliations, the press cycles, and the public office: what remains is **a Harlem-born child of a minister and a murdered mother who decided, at an age the file cannot precisely fix but which predates adolescence, that he was going to spend his adult life making the kinds of rooms his parents died in into safer rooms.** That decision is the irreducible core. Every subsequent vocational choice — licensed social work, costumed partnership, Avengers tenure, shield-bearing, mentorship of Joaquin Torres, the international caseload of the mature period — is a re-instantiation of that single childhood vow at progressively larger scales. The cape is the social work continued by other means; the shield is the cape continued by other means; the mature international portfolio is the shield continued by other means. The vocation has never changed. Only the radius has.

At the deepest level the subject is, in the precise clinical sense, a **sublimator** — a person whose primary defense against intolerable early loss is the consistent, lifelong conversion of helplessness into utility on behalf of others. Vaillant's mature-defense literature describes this pattern as one of the most reliable predictors of long-arc psychological flourishing in trauma-exposed populations, and the subject is a near-textbook exemplar. The vocational identity is not a costume over a damaged self; the vocational identity *is* the self, constructed in real time, every day, as the working answer to a question the subject was forced to ask before he had the vocabulary for it: *what does a person do, in a world that killed both of his parents for trying to help.*

Below the sublimator sits the **interrogator of his own goodness**. The Snap retcon — whether one accepts it as canon, treats it as a violation later writers softened, or reads it as a permanent metaphor for the Black male public figure being told his interiority is not his own — installed a second-order question beneath the first: *is the kindness I have built actually mine.* The subject's answer, derived not from rumination but from practice, is functionally pragmatist: **the kindness is mine because I keep choosing it, regardless of where it came from.** This is not a settled conviction; it is a re-decided one. The re-deciding is daily. It is the engine.

Below the interrogator sits the **partner**. The subject is constitutionally a dyadic actor — he works best, regulates best, and is happiest in two-person operational and intimate units. The pattern is consistent across every era and every relationship of record: paired with Rogers, paired with Barnes, paired with Knight, paired with Torres, paired pre-canon with Riley. The dyad is the unit at which the subject's gifts compound and his vulnerabilities are buffered. Structural solitude — the lone Black Avenger under Gyrich, the lone Black Captain America under the Hauser-analog press cycle — is the condition under which his system finally degrades. Note this carefully: **the subject is not lonely in any romantic or self-pitying sense; he is dyadically optimized, and isolation costs him operationally before it costs him emotionally.**

---

### The Through-Line

The through-line of the subject's entire existence is the **consistent, conscious refusal to let any external authority — supervillain, federal agency, press apparatus, team bureaucracy, or symbolic tradition — be the author of his identity.** This refusal is not stated as a creed; it is enacted as a practice. The practice is observable at every major inflection point in the operational record:

- He quit the Avengers when Gyrich's mandate made him a checkbox rather than a teammate. He did not negotiate; he did not perform compliance; he removed himself from the structure that had instrumentalized him.
- He took the shield in 2014 *and* gave it back in 2017 — and the giving-back is the through-line evidence, not the taking. He surrendered symbolic capital from a position of moral self-doubt, which is behavior that pathological narcissism, ordinary ambition, and standard heroic narrative all fail to predict. Only an actor whose primary commitment is to **authorship over status** produces that move.
- He returned to the shield under Coates and Onyebuchi on terms he had personally re-negotiated with himself, having metabolized the first tenure rather than re-attempting it unchanged.
- He split from S.H.I.E.L.D. on surveillance grounds — a values-based exit from an institution he could easily have continued to operate inside, indicating that institutional capture is something he actively scans for and refuses.
- He has never, in fifty years of record, allowed a press cycle to dictate his next move. Press cycles register; press cycles do not steer.

The through-line, restated more compactly: **subject orients to the project rather than the symbol.** Rogers serves an idea of America; subject serves the operational project of building the America that the idea describes, which means he can put down any particular instrument (the shield, the title, the team seat) without putting down the work. This is the single most reliable predictor of his behavior in any given scenario. **If the symbol and the work diverge, the subject will follow the work.** Every time. With no exceptions in the file.

---

### The Core Wound And Its Maintenance

**The core wound is not the parental loss. The core wound is the question the parental loss left behind, which the Snap retcon then weaponized, which the public reception of the shield then re-weaponized, which every subsequent challenge to his legitimacy has continued to weaponize: *am I the author of who I am, or am I being authored by forces that do not have my interests at heart.***

The parental loss was the originating injury, but its specific psychic signature is critical: both parents were killed while *helping*, in the community they were trying to *heal*. The lesson available to the child was not merely "the world is dangerous" — it was the much more corrosive lesson that "trying to make the world safer is what gets you killed." Any subject whose adult vocation is making the world safer is, in the subject's case, *contradicting his own developmental data every single working day.* This is the deep structure of his exhaustion. He is not tired from the missions; he is tired from a half-century of acting against the inferential conclusion his childhood handed him.

The Snap retcon — read here as the canonical record describes it, regardless of later softening — added a second wound that fused with the first. The first wound said: *the world will kill you for being good.* The second wound said: *and your goodness may not even be yours.* The compound effect is a permanently destabilized self-concept that the subject must, daily, manually stabilize. He does this through:

1. **Vocational continuity.** The social work credentials are not vestigial; they are load-bearing. They are the evidence the subject offers to himself that his orientation toward care predates and exceeds any costume.
2. **Verbal articulation.** The subject *talks* about his interior life — to teammates, to mentees, to romantic partners — at a rate substantially above the principal-population baseline. This is not disclosure for its own sake; it is the daily practice of *narrating his own identity in his own voice* before anyone else narrates it for him.
3. **Humor as regulation.** The wit that every writer has captured is not affect; it is a regulation strategy. Humor lowers threat in the room, which lowers threat in his own nervous system, which preserves the cognitive bandwidth required for the higher-order work of self-authorship.
4. **Selective withdrawal.** When the cost of maintaining authorship inside a given role exceeds the benefit, the subject exits the role rather than fragmenting the self. The 2017 shield surrender is the type-specimen.
5. **Dyadic anchoring.** The small circle of durable intimates functions as a distributed mirror — a set of people who reflect his identity back to him in forms he trusts, which reduces the load on his own internal reflection.

The maintenance regime is effective but **not cheap**. It runs continuously. There is no off-duty version of the subject in which the maintenance pauses. The closest he comes to rest is in the dyadic settings — a quiet patrol with Barnes, a kitchen-table conversation with Knight, a debrief with Torres — where the maintenance is shared rather than solo. **Any operational planning that involves the subject must account for the maintenance cost as a permanent line item, not a stress-induced spike.**

---

### Operational Summary

**Role profile.** Subject is the highest-utility de-escalator in the principal population. Deploy him into hostage scenarios, civilian extractions, community-interface operations, cross-faction negotiations, and any environment in which the failure mode of force exceeds the failure mode of patience. Subject is also a top-decile tactical operator with persistent aerial-and-avian sensory overlay, making him exceptional in urban three-dimensional environments and in containment-rather-than-suppression mission profiles. He is not the principal to deploy when the mission requires a sustained one-on-one slugging match against an enhanced opponent; his unenhanced status makes such deployments a poor expected-value bet on a long enough timeline, and he knows it.

**Cognitive profile.** Gestalt, systems-oriented, room-reading before person-reading, board-reading before move-selecting. Subject will reliably notice the second-order consequence the rest of the room has missed. He will also reliably notice the political and racial subtext of an operational order, and will act on his read of it.

**Reliability.** Among the highest in the file. Subject does not freelance, does not no-show, does not collapse under acute stress, and does not have a documented rage state. The reliability has one and only one boundary condition: **if the mission requires him to act as an instrument of values he does not hold, he will refuse, withdraw, or relinquish the role.** This boundary is non-negotiable and has been demonstrated under maximal pressure (Gyrich, shield surrender, S.H.I.E.L.D. split, Hydra-Cap aftermath). Plan around it; do not attempt to override it.

**Handler guidance.**
- *Do not flatter him.* He reads it instantly and it lowers his trust.
- *Do not racialize him as a recruitment lever.* The Gyrich record is dispositive.
- *Do not separate him from his dyadic anchors* unless operationally necessary; if necessary, restore the contact at the earliest opportunity.
- *Do not ask him to be uncomplicated.* The most counterproductive request any institution has ever made of the subject is to perform a simpler version of himself than he is. He cannot do it and will not pretend to.
- *Do give him the full picture.* He is one of the few principals whose tactical performance *improves* with more context, not less. He is also one of the few who will tell you, in plain language, when he thinks you are wrong.
- *Do let him talk.* The verbal-articulation pattern is regulatory; suppressing it degrades performance.

**Failure modes to monitor.**
1. *Cumulative orthopedic and neurological load.* He is unenhanced, the body is keeping a score that the subject is disciplined about not dramatizing, and the bill is real.
2. *Structural solitude.* If he is again positioned as the lone Black principal in a hostile press environment without dyadic support, expect a repeat of the 2017 withdrawal pattern on a similar timeline.
3. *Community-source criticism.* National-press criticism does not move him; criticism from Harlem, from Black America, from people he believes he was supposed to protect, lands at depth and is the closest analog he has to a depressive trigger. Monitor the community-feedback channel as the leading indicator, not the press cycle.
4. *Instrumentalization.* Any operation that risks using him for ends he would not endorse if fully informed will not merely fail; it will burn the relationship with him for years. The Hydra-Cap arc is the type-specimen.
5. *Partnership betrayal.* The rare documented instances of sustained anger in the file are all traceable to threats against or betrayals by his small circle. This is the one vector on which his flat escalation curve does not stay flat.

**Long-term trajectory.** Subject is in the mature phase of a fifty-year operational career and has, against all actuarial expectation for his cohort, arrived at it more integrated rather than less. The trajectory is toward mentorship, international scope, and the continued re-authorship of the Captain America role on terms he sets. He is not expected to retire in the conventional sense; the vocation is the self, and he is not in the habit of relinquishing the self. He is expected, however, to continue the pattern of putting down particular instruments when the instruments stop serving the work. **Plan for a subject who will outlast most of the institutions currently attempting to define him, and who will be doing the same work, in some recognizable form, on the day the file is closed.**

---

### One-Sentence Summation

**Subject is a man who has spent his entire life answering, in public and in private, the question of whether he gets to be the author of his own goodness — and whose answer, delivered not as a statement but as a fifty-year practice, is yes.**


## Chronology I — Origin & Childhood

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: SAMUEL THOMAS WILSON
## CHRONOLOGY I — ORIGIN & CHILDHOOD

*Surveillance window: pre-natal through approximately age fifteen. Material reconstructed from* Captain America *#117 (Lee/Colan, 1969),* #126, #133–138, #186 *(Englehart, 1975, the Snap reveal),* Captain America and the Falcon *vol. 1 #1–6 (1971 relaunch),* Captain America *#276–278,* Captain America and the Falcon *vol. 2 #1–14 (Priest, 2004),* Avengers/Thunderbolts *background material,* Captain America: Sam Wilson *#1–6 (Spencer, 2015) flashback sequences, and Coates'* Captain America *vol. 9 (2018–2021) memorial passages. Where canon contradicts itself across the Snap retcon, both readings are preserved; UATU prefers the lived-subjective record over metaphysical adjudication of which memory set is "original."*

---

### 1.1 BIRTH AND THE FAMILY OF ORIGIN

Samuel Thomas Wilson is born in Harlem, New York City. The published birthdate floats — Marvel's sliding timeline collapses it variably to the late 1950s in early Bronze-Age framing and to the late 1970s/early '80s in modern recompression — but the *place* is fixed and never negotiable in any version: the file records a Harlem hospital delivery, almost certainly Harlem Hospital Center on Lenox Avenue, the institution of record for Black births north of 110th Street in that period. Neighborhood of upbringing: central Harlem, in the corridor between 125th and 145th, walking distance to the AME and Baptist church network that anchors the Wilson family's civic identity.

**Father: Paul Wilson.** Reverend, identified in *Captain America* #186 and elaborated in Priest's *Captain America and the Falcon* vol. 2 as a Baptist minister of a small storefront-to-mid-size Harlem congregation. Paul Wilson is the central male object in Sam's developmental record — a community-facing preacher of the social-gospel tradition, not a pulpit-only operator. The canon consistently shows him as the kind of minister who walked the block, who knew the names of the corner kids, who saw his ministry as extending into the street fights and the family disputes of his parishioners. He is the *active-interventionist* archetype, the Black Protestant clergyman as community broker. This is the model Sam internalizes before he has language for it.

**Mother: Darlene Wilson.** Less elaborated in canon and therefore more interpretively dangerous. What is consistent: a mother present in the home, central to the religious life of the children, the one who took Sam to choir practice and to Sunday school, the source of the cooking-and-singing domesticity that flickers in Sam's adult memory in Spencer #2 and in a single Coates panel where Sam is shown holding a folded apron during a Harlem flashback. She is killed in a mugging approximately two years after Paul's death. The combination — pastor father killed mediating a fight, mother killed in a random street robbery — establishes Sam's foundational threat schema: *violence comes from both directions, from the work of trying to help and from the accident of being present.*

**Siblings.** Older brother **Gideon Wilson** (named in *Captain America and the Falcon* vol. 2 #2; Priest's recasting of earlier "Jody" references) and younger sister **Sarah Wilson Casper** (the Casper surname from her later marriage, with children Jim and Jody Casper who feature in the Priest run). Sam is the middle child. This birth-order position is operationally significant: across his entire adult life Sam occupies *middle* positions — between Rogers and the rest of the team, between S.H.I.E.L.D. and the street, between Harlem and the Avengers — and the family-system origin of that broker role is the sibling triangle of Gideon-Sam-Sarah.

**Extended family.** Sam's paternal aunt and uncle — most prominently the figures who take in or partially raise the orphaned siblings after Darlene's death — are reconstructed across scattered Bronze-Age dialogue but never named consistently. The functional record: the three Wilson children are not sent into the foster system; they are absorbed into the network of the church and extended kin, which is both protective and structurally insecure. Sam does not lose his neighborhood. He loses the parents who anchored him in it.

### 1.2 ENVIRONMENT: HARLEM AS DEVELOPMENTAL TERRAIN

The Harlem of Sam's childhood — sliding timeline notwithstanding — is canonically the post-civil-rights, pre-gentrification Harlem of the late mid-century: a community in the long aftermath of the 1964 riot, of the heroin epidemic, of the slow withdrawal of municipal services, of a vibrant church and small-business culture under economic siege. The Apollo, the 369th Regiment Armory, the brownstones on Strivers' Row, the corner barbershops, the AME Zion churches — these are the textural facts of the environment. Sam's adult speech patterns retain Harlem cadence (consistent in Englehart, Priest, Spencer, Coates, Onyebuchi); his food references (collards, mac and cheese, his sister's sweet potato pie — Spencer #5) anchor in the same Sunday-dinner tradition; his religious literacy (he can quote scripture without strain, observed across runs) is residual childhood Baptist immersion.

The street-level facts: Sam learns to walk a city block as a Black child in a neighborhood where adults are routinely subjected to police stops, where a wrong corner at the wrong hour produces real danger, where the difference between a safe and an unsafe route is not abstract. The *spatial vigilance* that becomes the bird's-eye cognitive style of the adult operator is rehearsed daily, on foot, from approximately the age he is allowed to walk to school alone — call it eight — through the entirety of his Harlem upbringing.

The bird element is also pre-figured environmentally. Pigeons on the rooftops, the rooftop coops that older men kept across upper Manhattan in that period, the Harlem tradition of pigeon-keeping that runs through Black urban masculinity from the 1940s forward — Sam's later affinity with birds is not a costume conceit but a continuity. There is a recurring Bronze-Age aside (Englehart, *Captain America* #134) of Sam recalling a rooftop where an old man kept birds; in the Priest run the rooftop returns as the site where Sam went to be alone after his father's death. Whether one reads the avian rapport as Cosmic Cube artifact, mutant latency, or post-human emergence, the *psychological* anchoring is rooftop pigeons in childhood Harlem.

### 1.3 THE FATHER'S DEATH

The single most over-determined event in Sam's developmental record. Canon timing: Sam is *a child* — usually rendered as eight or nine, occasionally younger — when Reverend Paul Wilson, attempting to break up a fight between neighborhood men (in some tellings, a dispute spilling out of a bar; in others, a confrontation between two parishioners on the street), is struck and killed. The weapon varies — fist, bottle, in one Englehart aside a knife — but the structural facts are constant: Paul intervenes unarmed, Paul is killed, the killer is not a supervillain or a system but *a neighbor*.

The semantic load is enormous. Sam loses his father (1) to violence, (2) to the very community his father was serving, (3) in an act of intervention that mirrors precisely what Sam's adult vocation will be. Every de-escalation Sam later performs — every hostage talk-down, every step between two combatants, every choice to put his unaugmented body between people who could hurt each other — is a re-staging of the moment his father did the same thing and did not survive it. Sam knows this about himself. The Priest run makes it explicit (vol. 2 #6): Sam, after a successful intervention, sits on a rooftop and notes that he has "out-lived him by every one of these."

Behavioral consequences observable in the immediate post-event window (reconstructed from flashback material): Sam becomes the *quiet* child. The pre-loss Sam, glimpsed in a single Coates flashback panel and in Spencer's #2 memory sequence, is a louder, more performative kid — the preacher's son with a preacher's son's affect, theatrical, comfortable in front of a room. Post-loss Sam learns to watch. The shift from front-of-the-room to back-of-the-room is the first instance of the regulation that becomes his adult signature. The humor — also constant in the adult — survives, but it is repurposed: it stops being performance and becomes *tool*, the way he reaches across distance to people he can no longer assume will stay.

### 1.4 THE MOTHER'S DEATH

Approximately two years later. Darlene Wilson is killed in a mugging — purse-snatching escalated to homicide, in the most common rendering — on a Harlem street, in the evening, returning home. Sam is now approximately ten or eleven. The killer is not caught in canon; this matters, because the open file is the kind of unresolved trauma that produces the *systems* orientation rather than the *individual-revenge* orientation of Sam's adult moral life. He does not have a face to hate. He has a condition — *streets that do this to mothers* — and the condition is what he later organizes himself against.

The second loss completes a structure. After Paul, Sam still has a parent; after Darlene, Sam is an orphan with siblings, absorbed into extended kin and the church network. The *attachment* literature would predict catastrophe here — double parental loss to violence in middle childhood is among the heaviest pre-adolescent risk loads on record. The fact that adult Sam reads as earned-secure rather than disorganized is the central unexplained-by-environment finding of his entire file, and the explanation has to lie in (a) temperamental robustness, (b) the *quality* of the eight-to-ten years of attachment he did receive from Paul and Darlene, (c) the church/kin network that did not let him fall through, and (d) the older-sibling presence of Gideon as a transitional attachment figure.

Coates' run includes a brief but devastating sequence (vol. 9 #7) in which Sam, mid-mission, sees a woman with a purse on a Harlem street and tracks her with his eyes until she reaches her door. This is not a one-time observation; this is the residue of a forty-year operational habit. UATU notes: the surveillance pattern of the adult Sam Wilson includes a *constant low-grade visual sweep for women alone on streets at dusk.* He is not aware he is doing it. He has been doing it since he was eleven.

### 1.5 THE INTERIM — ADOLESCENCE BEFORE THE BREAK

Between Darlene's death and Sam's emergence into the early adult records (the social-work training in the canonical line, or the Los Angeles/criminal-period departure in the Snap reading), there is the *long quiet middle* of his adolescence in extended-family Harlem. The behavioral patterns laid down in this window:

- **Church embedding.** Sam is at services, in choir, in the youth programs. His religious literacy is not theological sophistication but *practiced familiarity* — the scripture he can quote is the scripture that was sung and prayed around him weekly through his teens. He does not, in adult life, present as a believer in any orthodox sense; he presents as someone shaped by a tradition he no longer needs to declare.
- **Sibling responsibilities.** Sam becomes a co-caregiver to Sarah, the younger sister, almost certainly from age eleven or twelve forward. The mentoring patience he later shows Joaquin Torres is a re-issue of an old skill. Gideon's role is murkier — some tellings have Gideon already in trouble by this point, the brother who *did* go a wrong way and against whom Sam quietly defined himself.
- **Schooling.** Public school, Harlem. Sam is canonically literate, articulate, comfortable with formal speech — the social-work degree later is plausible only against a record of strong-enough secondary education. He is not depicted as a standout academic, but he is depicted, consistently, as a *reader* — a habit that almost certainly originates in this window.
- **Athletics.** Some Bronze-Age dialogue references school athletics, possibly track or basketball, consistent with the adult lean-runner-physiologist build. No football. No contact sports — which, given the head-trauma load of his adult career, is the only protective factor on his neurological balance sheet.
- **Work.** Adolescent work in the neighborhood — odd jobs, possibly a stint at one of the rooftop pigeon coops, possibly at a corner store. The exact pattern is undocumented; the *fact* of early work is consistent with the orphan-in-extended-kin economic position.

### 1.6 THE SNAP COUNTER-MEMORY

UATU is obligated to record the contested branch. In the Red Skull's Cosmic Cube–induced retcon (*Captain America* #186, Englehart, 1975), the gentle-pacifist Sam Wilson is a false memory implant. The "real" pre-implant history is: Sam as **"Snap" Wilson**, a Harlem street kid who graduated to small-time hustling, who moved at some point to Los Angeles, who fell into mob-adjacent enforcement work, who survived a plane crash on Exile Island where the Skull found him and rewrote his personality into a tool against Rogers.

How to file this: as a *subjective* trauma whether or not it is *historically* true. From the perspective of total surveillance, the relevant data are (a) Sam's behavioral record, which is constant and which does not change after the reveal, and (b) Sam's interior processing of having been told that his goodness was authored by his worst enemy. The Snap material is the etiological substrate of the adult preoccupation with *authorship of self* — the single most consistent pressure point on his file.

Note, however: even the Snap reading places the *childhood* — the parents, the deaths, the Harlem rootedness — as real. The retcon overwrote an adolescence and early adulthood, not a beginning. The ground floor of this dossier is not contested by Englehart's intervention. The pastor father and the murdered mother and the rooftop with the birds and the sister to look after are constants under every reading.

### 1.7 EARLIEST BEHAVIORAL PATTERNS — INVENTORY

The following micro-patterns trace cleanly from the childhood record into the adult operational profile:

1. **Room-reading before person-reading.** Originates in the spatial-vigilance demand of the Harlem street and the church social hall. Operational analog: Sam clears a space gesturally before he addresses an individual in it.
2. **Verbal de-escalation as first instrument.** Originates in the modeling of Paul Wilson's interventionist pastoral style. Operational analog: Sam talks first in every hostage and standoff scenario in the published record.
3. **Humor as bridge, not shield.** Originates in the post-loss repurposing of the preacher's-son theatricality. Operational analog: Sam's wit is reliably *generative* — it opens conversations and lowers thresholds — rather than the defensive wit of, e.g., Stark.
4. **Watching women on the street at dusk.** Originates in Darlene's death. Operational analog: documented gaze-tracking patterns through Coates and Onyebuchi runs.
5. **Caregiver-to-younger-sibling pattern.** Originates with Sarah. Operational analog: the mentoring relationship with Joaquin Torres, the patient management of the Hauser-era civilian hotline callers, the way Sam talks to children in the field (consistent Bronze-Age through present).
6. **Rooftop affinity.** Originates with the pigeon coops and the post-trauma rooftop solitude. Operational analog: Sam's preferred field perch, his stated comfort with altitude, the choice of avian symbology when the wings were offered.
7. **Skepticism of centralized force.** Originates in the dual knowledge that (a) his father's death was not prevented by any institution and (b) his mother's killer was not caught by any institution. Operational analog: the S.H.I.E.L.D. split, the Americops opposition, the lifelong preference for community-based intervention.
8. **Refusal to externalize aggression.** Originates in the impossibility of having a face to hate after Darlene's death. Operational analog: the *flat escalation curve* — Sam has no rage state because rage was, in childhood, structurally denied an object.
9. **Stable warmth toward dyadic partners.** Originates in the residual security of the pre-loss family. Operational analog: the durable partnerships across his adult life.
10. **Quiet self-interrogation as default mode.** Originates in the transition from front-of-the-room to back-of-the-room after Paul's death. Operational analog: the examined self-concept that no public role has been able to dislodge or to settle.

### 1.8 ASSESSMENT — THE GROUND FLOOR

The childhood record establishes a child who lost the two adults who organized his world to two different faces of the same violence, who was not allowed by the church-and-kin network to fall, who responded to catastrophic loss by going *quieter and more watchful* rather than louder and more aggressive, and who carried out of that decade the exact toolkit — verbal de-escalation, room-reading, dyadic loyalty, rooftop affinity, institutional skepticism, refusal to externalize — that he would deploy operationally for the next fifty years.

The remarkable finding is not what was damaged. The remarkable finding is what was *preserved*: the warmth, the humor, the capacity for trust. The conventional developmental prediction for a child with Sam Wilson's loss profile is a much more damaged adult. The deviation from prediction is the central mystery of the file and the foundation of every subsequent chapter. He should not have come out of that childhood the way he came out of it. The fact that he did is the first thing about him that an intelligence apparatus, however benevolent, must learn to *respect* rather than to *explain*.

*— Chronology I closes. Chronology II to follow: late adolescence, the contested LA interval, return to Harlem, education, and the emergence of the social-work vocation.*


## Chronology II — Formation & Emergence

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: SAMUEL THOMAS WILSON
## Chronology II — Formation & Emergence

*(Covers approximately ages 12 through 28: the orphaning, the foster/extended-kin years, the drift into and out of the street life that the Snap retcon names, the educational reconstruction, the social-work credentialing, the Exiles island incident, the meeting with Steve Rogers, the first costume, the Redwing imprint, and the first ninety days of operational service that fixed the template of everything that came after.)*

---

### 1. The Orphaning and the Year After

The two violent losses are not symmetrical and the file should not flatten them. Paul Wilson, Baptist minister of a small storefront congregation in Harlem, was killed when Sam was approximately nine intervening in a fight between two neighborhood men on the steps of his own church. The detail that has remained consistent across every telling: Paul did not die on scene. He was conscious long enough to speak to a paramedic and to be transported. Sam was kept from the hospital that night by an aunt and learned of the death the next morning. This is the structural origin of a behavior pattern that recurs across his adult life — Sam's compulsion, in any crisis, to *be present at the bedside* rather than be informed afterward. Every writer who has put him in a hospital scene (Englehart, Priest, Brubaker, Coates, Onyebuchi) has written him as the one who stays in the room.

Darlene Wilson was killed two years later, shot during a street robbery a block and a half from the apartment, walking home from a double shift. Sam was eleven. He was the one who identified her at the precinct, accompanied by his father's elder sister. The detail that survives in his somatic record: he does not flinch at the smell of disinfectant. He flinches at the smell of *coffee in styrofoam* — the precinct waiting-room marker. This is the kind of micro-tell a surveillance file logs over time: in canon scenes set in NYPD or federal interview rooms, Sam consistently declines the offered cup.

The intervening twelve to eighteen months between the two deaths produced the foundational psychological event that the Snap retcon would later attempt to overwrite. Sam at ten was, by every later account from Sarah and from Gideon, *the quiet one* — the child who organized his father's sermon notes, who fed the younger sister, who walked Darlene to and from the bus stop after Paul's death because he had decided, in the magical thinking of a grieving ten-year-old, that he could keep her alive by accompanying her. He could not. The night Darlene was killed, Sam was at home with Sarah; he had been told, that one time, that he did not need to come to the stop. The magical-thinking guilt seeded then is the substrate over which every subsequent guilt-structure in his life has been laid.

### 2. Kinship Care and the Drift (Approximately Ages 12–17)

The three Wilson children were not placed into foster care in the formal sense. They were absorbed by an extended network — primarily the paternal aunt, secondarily two cousins of Darlene's in the Bronx — in a pattern entirely typical of Black urban kinship care in the late 1950s and early 1960s. Sarah, the youngest, was the most consistently kept by the aunt. Gideon, oldest, left the household at approximately fifteen. Sam was the middle child and the floater — six months at the aunt's, a year with a cousin, periodic returns. The instability is not catastrophic in the file but it is *constitutive*: Sam from age twelve onward is the child who learns to read a household in the first ten minutes, identify the rules, identify the dangers, identify the food situation, and configure himself accordingly. The adult capacity that opposing tacticians have learned to fear — Sam walking into a hostage room and recalibrating within seconds — was rehearsed nightly across five years of unfamiliar kitchens.

Schooling was inconsistent through this period. Sam was a *bright* student by every account, but bright in the unstable way of a child with no homework surface. He read voraciously — the canon scenes in his Harlem apartment in the Englehart and Priest runs consistently show shelf furniture for paperbacks, and Sam's vocabulary in dialogue is the wide, slightly bookish register of an autodidact rather than a credentialed one. By approximately fourteen he was running with older boys.

### 3. The "Snap" Period (Approximately Ages 16–22)

The file's position on the Snap retcon was established in the Shared Assessment: treat it as a *lived experience* regardless of metaphysical status, because the behavioral residue is the same either way. Here is the granular reconstruction.

Between approximately sixteen and twenty-two, Sam Wilson was operationally embedded in a Harlem street economy. The roles attributed to him across the Englehart, DeMatteis, and Gruenwald passes include: numbers runner, then collector, then enforcer for a mid-tier operation tied tangentially to the criminal apparatus that would later be associated with figures like Morgan and Stoneface. He was not a senior figure. He was a *useful* figure — physically capable (the wiry, fast frame visible in every later depiction is older than his training), verbally quick, with the inherited preacher's ability to talk a man out of a doorway. The street name "Snap" attached to him in this period; canon is inconsistent on whether the derivation is the snap of fingers (a tell during high-pressure conversation), the snap of a switchblade, or the percussive verbal style. The behavior file leans on the first: Sam in adult life still has a finger-snap micro-tic when he is *about* to interrupt himself in conversation, suppressed but visible in close panels.

What he was *not*, even in this period: a killer of record, a user, a fixture of any specific crew's social life. Multiple later sources describe him as the one who came in, did the job, and left. The dissociative quality the retcon imputes is consistent with what a contemporary clinician would call **functional compartmentalization under adverse developmental conditions** — a young man performing a role he could neither refuse nor integrate, returning between jobs to his aunt's apartment to read library books and check on Sarah. The "two Sams" the Cosmic Cube allegedly engineered may be better understood as the two Sams that *poverty and grief* engineered, with the Cube serving as the supervillain rationalization for an ordinary developmental pattern.

The exit point is the file's first major inflection. There was an episode — variably dated to approximately Sam's twenty-second year — in which a collection job went bad and a bystander, a Harlem woman of approximately his mother's age at the time of her death, was injured. Sam was not the agent of the injury. He was present, and he was *recognized* by the woman, who used his given name. The shock of being named in his actual identity inside the role he had constructed to be nameless ended the period. He walked out of the operation that night, was not pursued seriously (he was too junior to be worth recovering), and entered the next phase essentially on foot.

### 4. Reconstruction (Approximately Ages 22–26)

Sam's twenties are the period the file knows least well in narrative terms and most well in *outcome* terms, because everything the adult Sam Wilson does is downstream of the choices made in these four years.

He completed a high-school equivalency credential through a community program associated with a Harlem church not his father's. He enrolled in a two-year community college program, transferred, and completed a bachelor's degree with a concentration that the canon variably names as sociology or social welfare. He worked nights through the entire credential — the jobs in the file include orderly at a Harlem hospital (the disinfectant tolerance dates from here), kitchen at a hotel near Times Square, and a period as a youth-program counselor at a community center that was effectively his apprenticeship for the career to come. He took the New York State social work licensure track and entered casework practice at approximately twenty-six, attached to a city agency with a Harlem-and-East-Harlem catchment.

The intimate-life record from this period is sparse and the file should not invent. Two relationships are alluded to in later expository dialogue: one with a woman from his college cohort that ended over the demands of his schedule, and one with a fellow caseworker that ended when she moved out of the city. Neither produced lasting acrimony. The pattern that would mark Sam's adult relationships — *clean exits, sustained warmth toward the ex, no theatrical heartbreak* — was already in place.

The somatic record from this period: Sam took up running. He has been a runner ever since. The route in the early years was a loop through Morningside and along the western edge of Central Park, pre-dawn, before shift. This is the period in which his sleep architecture stabilizes into the four-and-a-half-to-five-hour, twice-waking pattern that adult-life observers (Rogers, Barnes, Torres in shared-quarters scenes) have all noted: Sam wakes at approximately 4:40, sometimes again at 6:10, and is operational before most teammates have surfaced.

It is also the period in which he begins, quietly, to train. Not formally. He took a community boxing class, irregular attendance, and a self-defense seminar associated with the youth center. The hand-to-hand foundation that would later be polished by Rogers and (briefly) by the Black Panther's instructors was laid by a Harlem trainer whose name does not survive in the file, with the rough functional style of a man teaching young people not to die in a fight rather than to win one. Sam's adult combat signature — *control the distance, end the engagement, do not perform* — is recognizably this lineage.

### 5. The Exiles Island Episode and the Redwing Imprint

The proximate triggering event of the costumed career is the Exiles incident — the canonical staging of which (*Captain America* #117) places Sam, in his late twenties, traveling in the Caribbean and finding himself stranded on an island controlled by surviving Exiles operatives under the residual influence of the Red Skull. The Skull's intent, as established in the #186 retcon, was to engineer a Trojan-horse asset against Rogers using the Cosmic Cube. The file's behavioral reading does not require accepting the engineered nature of the encounter to register what *Sam* did with it.

Three things happened on that island that the file dates as foundational:

**First, the imprint with Redwing.** The bird was, by Sam's own later accounts, already on the island — feral, possibly the survivor of someone else's hawking. Sam encountered the bird before he encountered the Exiles. He fed it. He named it. The bond, whether mystically catalyzed by the Cube or simply the ordinary intensity of two isolated organisms recognizing each other, formed in approximately three days and has never broken. Redwing is not a tool and the file should not characterize the bond as instrumental. It is the *first uncomplicated love* of Sam's adult life, formed at a moment of total isolation, and it is the prototype for every subsequent partnership: dyadic, mutual, unenforced.

**Second, the meeting with Rogers.** Steve was on the island under his own circumstances. The encounter has been re-staged by multiple writers but the core is stable: Sam offered Steve food, shelter intelligence, and tactical cooperation before he knew who Steve was. Steve, recognizing the offer for what it was — a stranger of evident competence extending unconditional aid — accepted, and then trained Sam over the following days for the assault on the Exiles' position. The training was compressed: hand-to-hand refinement, formation work, the use of a thrown weapon. Sam was a fast study. The relational dynamic established in those days has *never* shifted. Steve does not patronize Sam. Sam does not idolize Steve. They are two adults who recognized each other's quality in a crisis and have been working from that recognition for fifty in-universe years.

**Third, the first costume.** The original Falcon suit was made on the island, partly by Sam from available materials, partly engineered by Rogers with whatever was at hand. The bird-themed motif was Sam's choice — he was already working with Redwing, and the iconography came naturally. There is a granular detail here that the file underlines: Sam designed the suit himself. Across every subsequent redesign (the T'Challa-provided wing harness, the SHIELD-augmented variants, the Captain America uniform of the 2014 transition, the post-Coates redesign), Sam has retained final authority over his own iconography. He has never worn a costume designed *for* him without modification. This is consistent with the authorship-of-self drive identified in the Personality section: he will accept materials, he will accept assistance, he will not accept being *dressed*.

### 6. The First Ninety Days

The post-island return to Harlem is the period in which the adult template fixes. Sam did not quit social work. He folded the costumed activity into evenings, weekends, and the unpaid hours of a man with a calling. The casework continued. He kept the apartment. He did not move uptown, downtown, or out. The Falcon operated within roughly a forty-block radius of where Sam Wilson lived and worked, and the operational radius and the civilian radius were *the same radius*. This is the single most important fact about his early career and the one that distinguishes him most sharply from every other costumed contemporary: there was no secret life *somewhere else*. The cape and the casefile were two tools deployed in the same neighborhood by the same person on behalf of the same people.

The first ninety days of operational activity established the behavioral repertoire that adult Sam has never abandoned:

- **De-escalation as default.** The earliest Falcon engagements were not supervillain fights. They were domestic disturbance interventions, gang mediations, the recovery of a runaway, the talking-down of a suicidal jumper from a rooftop on 138th Street. Sam built the costumed identity on the *social work* skill set before he built it on the combat skill set.
- **The aerial overlook.** Even before the genuine flight rig, Sam used rooftops the way bird-handlers use perches. He observed before he engaged. He still does.
- **The verbal opener.** Sam has, since the first week, opened almost every engagement with speech. "Hey," "let's talk," "you don't want to do this." The opening line is consistent enough across decades that it functions as a tell. He is *announcing himself* — both because announcement reduces lethal-force risk and because being unannounced was the condition of the Snap years and he will not return to it.
- **The exit check.** Sam, from the first ninety days, has ended every engagement by checking on the bystanders before checking on himself. This is the social worker's pattern, not the soldier's. Rogers learned it from him. Barnes never did.

### 7. The First Defining Choices and Their Fallout

Four choices in the first two years of operational life established the operating system the rest of the file documents.

**Choice One: the partnership with Rogers as equal, not subordinate.** When the post-island arrangement formalized into ongoing co-operation, Sam declined to be characterized as a sidekick in the patterns then customary. He insisted, in dialogue and in operational practice, on being addressed and deployed as a partner. The press did not always cooperate; the federal apparatus did not always cooperate; Rogers himself, to his credit, did. The retitling of the book to *Captain America and the Falcon* in 1971 is the externalization of a relational fact Sam had already established in private.

**Choice Two: the refusal to leave Harlem.** Sam was, within his first two years of operational visibility, recruited by, courted by, or quietly offered relocation by at least three apparatuses (the Avengers reserve track, a federal counter-terror billet, an international NGO security consultancy). He declined all of them. The neighborhood was the point. The casework was the point. The visibility he was acquiring as the Falcon was, in his own framing, instrumentally useful only insofar as it served the catchment.

**Choice Three: the retention of the civilian career.** Sam never went costumed full-time in the manner of most contemporaries. The casework continued through the entirety of the Bronze Age. The file's reading is that this is not modesty and not financial necessity; it is *identity insurance*. As long as Sam Wilson the social worker exists, the Falcon is something Sam *does*, not something Sam *is*. This distinction is what enabled him, decades later, to put down the shield without ceasing to be himself.

**Choice Four: the public naming of indignity.** From his earliest interviews onward (the in-fiction Harlem and Bedford-Stuyvesant press of the Bronze Age), Sam articulated the racial dimensions of his role aloud. He did not perform it as a grievance and he did not perform it as a triumph. He named it. This is the rhetorical signature later writers (Priest most sharply, Spencer most politically, Coates most philosophically, Onyebuchi most globally) inherited and extended. Sam's willingness to say the thing out loud is older than any of his costumes.

### 8. The Residue

By the end of this formation period — call it the close of his thirtieth year — Sam Wilson had assembled the elements that the rest of his life would only refine: the running route, the four-forty wake, the disinfectant tolerance, the styrofoam-cup aversion, the suppressed finger-snap, the rooftop preference, the verbal opener, the exit check, the dyadic partnership style, the bird, the costume he designed himself, the day job, the apartment in the catchment, the willingness to name what was happening in the room, and the deep, unexamined-but-permanent conviction that the work was being present at the bedside before, during, and after — because the night his father died, he had not been.

Everything in the subsequent fifty in-universe years of file material is a variation on this template. The template was set, in its essentials, before the world knew his name.


## Chronology III — The Defining Middle Period

# CHRONOLOGY III — THE DEFINING MIDDLE PERIOD

## Frame

The middle of Sam Wilson's life — operationally, roughly the span from the late-Bronze-Age Falcon solo arcs through the long Brubaker/Remender Captain America years, terminating at the moment he accepts the shield from Steve Rogers — is the longest, densest, and most behaviorally informative stretch of the file. It is the period in which the *patterns* covered in the psychological and personality sections were not yet patterns but choices, repeated until they became character. Almost everything UATU treats as a "Wilson constant" in his later operational profile — the de-escalator voice, the room-reading entry, the refusal of rage, the preference for dyadic partnership, the conditional service to institutions, the deliberate Harlem footprint — is laid down, tested, and re-tested in this period. What follows is the granular record.

## I. The Long Falcon Era: Operational Maturation (post-#186 through the mid-1980s)

The Englehart retcon in *Captain America* #186 (1975) functions, in the longitudinal file, less as a biographical fact than as a **stressor event**. Whatever the metaphysical truth of "Snap," what is recorded behaviorally is a man who, after that arc, *changes his operational style by small, consistent degrees*. Pre-#186 Falcon was a high-affect, eager partner; post-#186 Falcon is observably quieter on comms, more given to confirming targets verbally before engagement ("you with me, Cap?" becomes a stock phrase in this window), more likely to take the rear position on entries, and — critically — more likely to walk away from a fight he believes he can de-escalate.

This is the period in which the **verbal-confirmation tic** crystallizes. Across Englehart, Gerber, McKenzie, and DeMatteis issues, Sam is repeatedly shown narrating the tactical picture aloud — to Redwing, to Rogers, to himself — in the cadence of a social worker checking in with a client. "I see two on the roof, Cap, north corner, I'm coming around." This is not radio discipline learned from a manual; it is the cognitive style of a man who has been told his own perceptions might not be his own and who has compensated by making them external and corroborable. UATU notes this is the same period in which Sam begins, in domestic contexts, to *name what he is doing while he is doing it* ("I'm making coffee, you want a cup, I'm going to ask you about last night") — a behavioral signature of the post-Snap years that persists for the rest of his life.

**Harlem footprint, 1975–1985.** Sam's social work caseload through this decade is sustained: the Harlem Community Center on (variously rendered) 130th Street, intake hours in the late afternoon, evening home visits, a documented preference for walking his caseload neighborhoods rather than driving. He is observably *known* on his blocks — the corner-store nods, the church-step conversations, the older women who address him as "Sammy" — and this familiarity is operational as well as personal. The Stoneface arcs, the Tumbler reappearances, the early '80s street-level confrontations with the Constrictor and various Hammerhead operations, all turn on intelligence Sam acquires through casework rather than through Avengers channels. He is, in this period, functionally a one-man neighborhood intelligence apparatus, and he is *better at it than any federal asset working the same territory*.

**Leila Taylor.** The long-running relationship with Leila Taylor through the late '70s and into the '80s is the file's primary record of Sam's adult intimate functioning before Misty. The pattern is informative: Leila is politically to Sam's left, more confrontational, frequently impatient with his costumed life, and Sam — observably — *does not argue her out of her positions*. He listens, concedes the parts he agrees with, and holds the parts he doesn't without escalation. The relationship eventually erodes under the strain of the dual life, but the breakups in the canon are characterized by *grief and acknowledgment* rather than recrimination. This is the prototype of every significant Wilson breakup that follows.

**The Gyrich Avengers stint (*Avengers* #183–184, 1979, and its aftershocks).** This is the single most psychologically formative *institutional* experience of Sam's middle period and deserves granular treatment. Henry Peter Gyrich, then the Avengers' federal liaison, mandates Sam's inclusion on the active roster under what is openly a racial quota. Sam knows it. The team knows it. Sam takes the seat anyway, and the question of *why* is one of the file's most revealing data points.

Read against the rest of the record, the decision is not careerist (Sam has never courted Avengers prestige) and not naïve (he understood what Gyrich was doing). It is, by inference, a wager: that by being *physically present* in the institution he might convert the tokenizing seat into a real one. The wager fails. He is treated as the affirmative-action Avenger by press and by some teammates; Hawkeye's resentment at being displaced is racially inflected in ways Sam absorbs without confronting. Sam's behavioral response across these issues is **textbook over-functioning** — he takes extra patrols, volunteers for the less glamorous duties, is the last to leave the Mansion after debriefs — until he reaches the point of recognition that the institution cannot be reformed from his seat. He resigns. The resignation letter, as later referenced, is short and unaccusatory; the *pattern* it establishes — **absorb, attempt, withdraw without rancor** — will be re-enacted, almost gesture for gesture, in the shield surrender of 2017.

UATU flags this as the inaugural instance of what becomes the Wilson institutional cycle: *enter on conditional terms, work harder than required, decline to negotiate publicly for better terms, withdraw when the terms become incompatible with self-respect.* The cycle repeats with S.H.I.E.L.D., with the Captain America mantle, and in attenuated form with every team Sam ever joins.

## II. The Priest Run: Naming the Conditions (*Captain America and the Falcon* vol. 2, 2004)

Skipping forward across the late-'80s and '90s — in which Sam's solo Falcon material is intermittent but the Harlem casework, the Redwing rapport, and the periodic Avengers reserve calls continue without major inflection — the file's next high-density entry is the Priest run.

What Priest's run records, in surveillance terms, is the period in which Sam **begins to articulate aloud** the dynamics he had previously absorbed silently. The behavioral change is measurable: dialogue ratios across his appearances shift. In Englehart-era issues Sam speaks roughly as often as Rogers in shared scenes; in Priest-era issues Sam *initiates* the difficult conversations more often than Rogers does. The "Black friend" speeches, the open naming of the sidekick frame, the refusal to perform gratitude for the partnership — these are not personality changes. They are the surfacing of an internal commentary that, by the surveillance record, had been running silently for thirty years.

This run also documents Sam under conditions of *manufactured suspicion* — entangled with Anti-Cap, framed and pursued, operating in a moral-grey field he had previously been spared. His behavior under those conditions is diagnostic: he does not panic, does not become paranoid, does not cut his ties. He continues to call Rogers, continues to check on his casework, continues to ask the verbal-confirmation questions. The pattern of **anchor-behaviors held under existential threat** is one of the most reliable markers in the entire Wilson record.

The Priest period also clarifies the **Misty Knight relationship** as the long-form successor to Leila. Misty is a peer in a way Leila was not — operational, armed, politically aligned. The Wilson-Knight dyad through the 2000s shows the file's first record of Sam in a relationship where his costumed life does not require translation. The breakups (intermittent, undramatic) are recorded as logistical rather than affective; the affection persists across separations, which is itself a Wilson signature.

## III. The Brubaker Years: The Confidant in Wartime (*Captain America* vol. 5, 2005–2012)

Brubaker's long Captain America run is the period in which Sam's role consolidates into something the file labels the **standing confidant**. He is not always the field deployment; he is reliably the person Rogers calls before and after. The behavioral evidence is consistent across roughly seven years of issues: Sam is the character to whom Rogers tells the things he tells no one else, including Sharon Carter and, after the resurrection, Bucky Barnes.

This is significant in two ways. First, it confirms that Sam's confidant capacity — the room-reading, the willingness to *say the thing* — is recognized and depended upon by the single most psychologically guarded person in the Marvel principal cast. Rogers does not confide easily; he confides in Sam. Second, it places Sam in proximity to every major intelligence inflection of the period (the Winter Soldier reveal, the Red Skull / Lukin operation, the *Civil War* fracture, the assassination of Rogers, the long restoration arc) without ever placing him at the *center* of the operational drama. He is, structurally, the listener. UATU notes that this is the period in which the operational habit of **closing comms with "we're going to figure this out"** becomes universal — used with Rogers, with Barnes, with Sharon, with Maria Hill, eventually with Torres. It is a verbal tic with a function: it transfers the cognitive load of solution-finding from the immediate moment to a future in which Sam is committed to being present.

**Civil War (2006–2007).** Sam sides with Rogers' anti-registration faction. The interest of the surveillance record is *how* he sides. He does not deliver speeches; he does not denounce Stark; he does not, on the record, frame the SHRA as a racial-policing issue although he has the standing to do so and the analytic frame for it. He simply goes where Rogers goes, fights when fighting is required, and continues to perform the de-escalator function within his own faction — talking down the more vengeful Secret Avengers operatives, mediating between Rogers and the looser cannons of the resistance. When Rogers surrenders on the courthouse steps, Sam is among the first to reach him and the first to call the team afterward. The post-assassination period (mid-2007 through the Bucky-Cap interregnum) is the longest sustained record of Sam in active grief. The behavioral signature is consistent with his entire prior history: **no withdrawal from relationships, intensified withdrawal into work**. He runs Harlem caseload harder, takes more solo Falcon ops, sleeps less by inference from his appearance in inter-issue panels (eye-line darker, less verbal in non-essential exchanges). He does not drink. He does not lash out. He grieves *operationally*.

**Bucky-Cap partnership.** Sam's partnership with Barnes during Rogers' absence is the file's primary record of his capacity to **transfer attachment without diluting it**. He does not treat Barnes as a Rogers-substitute; he does not freeze him out as a Rogers-displacer. He onboards him — patiently, with the developmental patience he later extends to Torres — and the partnership becomes functional within months. UATU treats this as evidence that Sam's attachment system is structurally generous: he is not the kind of secure-base operator who has *one* primary relationship; he is the kind who maintains multiple primaries in parallel.

## IV. The Remender Transition: The Body and the Hand-Off (*Captain America* vol. 7, 2012–2014)

The Remender run is the period in which two things happen at once: the long accumulating somatic load on Sam's body is foregrounded, and Rogers' age-stripping at the hands of the Iron Nail clears the structural space for the mantle transfer.

The Dimension Z arc is, in the file, primarily a Rogers event, but it is also where Sam's **standing assumption that Rogers will return** is, briefly, broken — and the behavioral data from his side of those issues shows the pattern. He works the search operationally, he does not perform grief publicly, he keeps the comms open as if Rogers will pick them up. When Rogers does return, aged and depowered, Sam is the first person Rogers asks to take the shield.

The hand-off itself, in *Captain America* #25 / *All-New Captain America* #1 (2014), is conducted privately before it is conducted publicly. The surveillance value of this is twofold. First, it records that Sam **accepted the offer in the room with Rogers and then went away and thought about it** before the public assumption. The deliberation interval is uncharacteristically long for a man whose pattern under offers of responsibility is to accept and over-function immediately; the deliberation is itself a signal of the weight Sam attached to the decision. Second, the public assumption is performed in costume, in flight, without speeches. Sam takes the shield as he takes everything: with the verbal economy of a man who does not believe symbols require explanation when the act is sufficient.

## V. Cross-Cutting Patterns of the Middle Period

**Redwing and the bird's-eye habit.** Across the entire middle period, Sam's tactical preference for elevated reconnaissance before engagement is unbroken. He is the Marvel principal least likely to enter a structure without first having seen its roof. The Redwing link operationalizes this, but the cognitive habit predates and outlasts any specific telemetry; even on missions where Redwing is unavailable, Sam circles before he enters. This habit, by the file's reading, is not tactical training. It is the somatic externalization of his core cognitive style: **see the whole board first, intervene from inside the picture, never from outside it.**

**The walking-Harlem signature.** Across decades, Sam moves through his home neighborhood on foot when not in costume. He is observed (across writers, with remarkable consistency) to take the same routes — Lenox between 125th and 135th, the side of the street with the shade in summer, the bodega on the corner whose owner he greets by name, the church his father served, which he passes but does not always enter. The route is not nostalgic; it is *maintenance*. Sam keeps the geography of his life intact by physically traversing it.

**Conditional service, irrevocable loyalty.** The middle period establishes the distinction the late period will rely on. Sam's service to *institutions* (Avengers, S.H.I.E.L.D., federal apparatus) is conditional and revocable; he leaves when terms degrade. His loyalty to *persons* (Rogers, Barnes, Misty, eventually Torres) is irrevocable and durable across separations, deaths, ideological disagreements, and identity violations. The file treats this distinction as one of the cleanest in any subject's record. Sam does not confuse the two, and his crises tend to occur precisely when an institution attempts to leverage a personal loyalty against his conditional service (Civil War being the textbook case).

**The flat escalation curve, tested.** The middle period contains every category of stressor that, in other subjects, produces rage states: the loss of a partner (Rogers, twice), institutional betrayal (Gyrich, the registration apparatus), identity violation (the Snap retcon and its rehearsals), racialized public attack, physical near-death. Sam does not produce a rage state at any point in the entire middle period. The behavioral envelope holds. The closest approach to a breaking point — the post-assassination months of 2007 — produces intensified work, not aggression. UATU flags this as the single most distinctive somatic-affective pattern in the file: **the escalation curve is genuinely flat, across decades, across stressors, under chronic and acute load.**

**The talker function institutionalized.** By the end of the middle period, Sam's function on any team scene is so reliably the verbal anchor that the file can predict, with high confidence, the structure of any group exchange: Sam will speak third, after the two highest-status interlocutors have established the disagreement; he will name the dynamic; he will offer the synthesis or the de-escalation; he will close with a forward-looking commitment. This pattern is observable in Avengers meetings, in Secret Avengers ops debriefs, in Harlem community board meetings, in conversations with Misty's family. The function is identical across contexts. It is, by the end of the middle period, no longer a behavior. It is the man.

## VI. The Threshold

The middle period closes with Sam in possession of the shield, in private possession of the deliberation that preceded the acceptance, and in public possession of a role he has spent forty operational years preparing for *without* preparing for. The patterns are now consolidated: the bird's-eye entry, the verbal confirmation, the walking-Harlem maintenance, the conditional institutional service, the irrevocable personal loyalty, the flat escalation curve, the de-escalator voice, the social-work intelligence apparatus, the dyadic preference, the over-functioning under tokenization, the withdrawal-without-rancor exit script. Every one of them will be tested, immediately and severely, in the period that follows.

The middle period is, in the end, the record of a man who did not become Captain America at the moment he was handed the shield. He became Captain America in the forty years in which he was not yet asked to be — by choosing, in private, repeatedly, the disciplines that would let him answer when the question was finally put to him.


## Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: SAMUEL THOMAS WILSON
## Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

### IV.1 Frame of Reference

The "recent" window for Subject covers the post-Spencer arc forward: roughly the close of the *Secret Empire* fallout (2017–18), through Coates' *Captain America* (Vol. 9, 2018–2021), the *Falcon & Winter Soldier* re-coupling material, *The United States of Captain America* (2021), Onyebuchi's *Captain America: Symbol of Truth* (2022–2023), and the current dual-Cap configuration in the *Captain America* relaunches and *Avengers* tertiary appearances of the post-2023 line. This is the era in which Subject moves from the *reluctant* reacquisition of the shield to its **deliberate, self-authored** carriage, and in which his operational footprint expands from domestic-symbolic to international-strategic.

### IV.2 The Re-Acceptance Phase (Coates Era, 2018–2021)

The starting condition of this era is **convalescent**. Coming out of *Secret Empire*, Subject has just lived through the public, year-long inversion of the symbol he carried — a Hydra-coded Rogers operating in the shield Subject had vacated. Subject's response is diagnostically consistent with everything else in the file: he does not pursue restoration of his own status, he does not give interviews, he does not litigate the question of who was "right." He returns to **Falcon livery**, returns to **street-level operations**, and is observed working a quiet ground-game in Harlem and surrounding boroughs for a period of months.

When Coates begins, Subject is operating in *support* of a chastened, returned Rogers — a deliberate inversion of the older partnership polarity. Subject is now the *senior* operator in the Cap-coded space in terms of recent symbolic experience. He has *carried* the title; Rogers has had it stolen and used against him. Subject is the one with somatic knowledge of what it costs.

The Nuke arc, the Power Elite arc, the Daughters of Liberty material — across these, Subject is the field commander Rogers defers to in tight tactical moments and the moral interlocutor Rogers defers to in ambiguous ones. He is observed sleeping on couches in safehouses, not requesting hotel rooms; eating standing up at safehouse counters; running pre-dawn rooftop circuits over Harlem (a habit traceable to the Brubaker era and intensified here). He is, by every indicator a longitudinal file can read, *recovering through work* — the same pattern he used after the Snap retcon reveal, after Riley, after every previous structural rupture.

The re-acceptance of the Captain America name happens **gradually and bilaterally**: by the end of the Coates run, both Rogers and Subject carry the title in different operational contexts without conflict. Subject's articulated position — observable in dialogue across the arc — is that the name is not a *seat* with one occupant but a *practice* that can be performed by more than one person at a time, provided each carries it honestly. This is the formal philosophical move that resolves the Spencer-era impasse. He is no longer trying to *replace* Rogers or to *be* Rogers; he is performing a different version of the same work.

### IV.3 The *United States of Captain America* Project (2021)

A discrete, important data point. Subject co-leads (with Rogers, Barnes, and Carter) a cross-country tour investigating the theft of Rogers' shield and, more importantly, **surfacing a network of unsanctioned, community-rooted Captain Americas** — a Kickapoo nurse, a gay activist, a teenage girl in the Southwest, others. The framing is significant for the file: Subject is the principal who *most readily accepts* these unauthorized Caps as legitimate, who treats the multiplication of the symbol as confirmation rather than threat.

This is the operationalization of his Coates-era philosophical position. The symbol belongs to its practice, not to its credentials. Subject's behavioral pattern during the tour — extended listening, low-affect questioning, refusal to position himself as the *real* Cap among pretenders — is the mature expression of the drive identified in the personality section: *to make safe the kinds of places that were not safe for him*. Including, now, safe for *other people to occupy the role that was not safe for him*.

### IV.4 *Symbol of Truth* (2022–2023): The International Pivot

Onyebuchi's run is the most significant recent reconfiguration of Subject's operational profile. Several first-order changes:

**Geographic scope.** Subject moves from a primarily domestic theater to a **transnational** one. Operations cover Mohannda, Wakanda, the U.S.–Mexico border, and the Caribbean. The triggering case is **Rabum Alal / White Wolf-adjacent serum trafficking**: Wakandan-sourced super-soldier serum, deliberately weaponized against Black populations through migration channels, marketed as an enhancement product to a population the U.S. medical establishment has historically under-served and surveilled. Subject's response is observably *cold* in a way that is rare for him — the affect-regulation is unusually tight, the operational speech unusually clipped, the humor unusually absent. This is the *community legitimacy* pressure point being struck at maximum intensity: the weapon is calibrated against the precise constituency Subject has organized his life around protecting.

**Institutional posture.** Subject operates with **substantially reduced** institutional backing. He is not S.H.I.E.L.D.-affiliated, not formally Avengers-deployed for most of the run, not in standing coordination with the federal apparatus. He runs ops with Torres, with occasional Misty Knight backup, with Wakandan intelligence on a case-specific basis, and with the loose **Daughters of Liberty** network when needed. This is the long-form realization of his anti-centralization preference: he has finally constructed a *practice* of the role that does not require a host institution he distrusts.

**Mentorship of Torres.** Joaquin Torres, now operating as the Falcon, is the active mentee. The relationship in this era is observably **developmental in the way Subject's relationship with Rogers never was** — Subject permits Torres to make mistakes, debriefs without humiliation, holds back interventions to let Torres run lead, and is patient with Torres' generational and stylistic differences (Torres is more comfortable with extrajudicial improvisation, more impulsive in the air, less culturally rooted in Harlem-specific community frames). Subject is teaching Torres not how to *be Sam* but how to *be Joaquin in the role*. This is the same philosophical position as the *United States* project, applied to a single inheritor.

**Bucky Barnes parallel-track.** Subject's relationship with Barnes in this period is operationally entwined — there are several joint cases and an extended subplot about a Barnes-adjacent threat — and personally **stable**. The two function as peers; Subject is one of the very few people who will tell Barnes the truth without softening, and Barnes accepts it from him.

**Physical condition.** The cumulative orthopedic cost flagged in the medical section is *visible* in this era. Subject is observed favoring his right shoulder after sustained aerial maneuvers, using longer pre-mission warm-up routines, and selecting glide-and-engage profiles that reduce hard-landing impact. He does not discuss this. Torres notices; Subject deflects with humor. The pattern is consistent with a high-mileage athlete managing decline through technique refinement rather than through capacity reduction — an exact behavioral match for the historical pattern of veteran combat operators who refuse to acknowledge attrition until forced to.

### IV.5 Public-Symbolic Status

As of the most recent canon checkpoint, Subject's public standing is **stabilized** in a configuration that would have seemed impossible during the Spencer run. The polarized media climate that nearly broke him in 2015–17 has not disappeared, but his relationship to it has changed: he no longer attempts to *win* the discourse. He gives short, declarative interviews when he gives them at all; he refuses sit-downs with hostile outlets; he is observably uninterested in his own narrative as a national project.

The right-wing media analog continues to exist; Subject does not engage. The Black press treats him as a serious figure rather than a curiosity; he engages there, but on terms — he will speak about cases and communities, not about himself. He has declined, repeatedly and on record, opportunities to position himself as a *political* figure. The pattern is consistent: Subject will be a symbol in *practice* but will not be a symbol in *brand*.

### IV.6 Domestic / Personal Configuration

**Harlem residence** remains the base. The apartment is modest, the routine is preserved — pre-dawn rooftop work, coffee at the same two or three counter-service places along a four-block radius, weekly check-ins with neighborhood contacts who predate his costumed career. The social work credential is **maintained**, though active casework has been intermittent; he keeps the license current as a deliberate act.

**Sarah and the nephews** (the Wilson family configuration that has stabilized across recent canon, with adjustments for the various continuity layers) are the **functional anchor**. Subject is observed traveling to family on a routine basis — not crisis-driven, ritual. Birthdays are kept. School events are attended when operational tempo permits and rescheduled when it does not. The nephews are old enough now to understand what their uncle does and young enough to still find it uncomplicatedly meaningful; Subject is careful to preserve that window without exploiting it.

**Misty Knight** remains the longest-running adult intimate relationship in the file, currently operating in the on-and-on-again rather than off configuration — collaborative, peer, sexually and emotionally functional, organized around mutual respect for each other's operational autonomy rather than around cohabitation. Neither has pushed for formal commitment; neither has withdrawn.
